SANSKRIT MANUSCRIPTS FROM TIBET
1 Vimalaprabhā commentary on the Kālacakra-tantra

INTERNATIONAL ACADEMY OF INDIAN CULTURE
and ADITYA PRAKASHAN, NEW DELHI



PREFACE
The present volume is a facsimile edition of two ancient Sanskrit manuscripts from Tibet, which
were actually used by Indian scholars and Tibetan lotsavas for translation into Tibetan. They are
valuable for the comments of the lotsavas written in the cursive Tibetan script dbu.med on the
palmleaves themselves. The two texts are: (i) Vimalaprabhā commentary on the Kālacakra-tantra
(KT), and (ii) Pañcarakṣā.
The Vimalaprabhā was translated into Tibetan by Somanātha of Kashmir and Šes.rab.grags the
Lotsava of Hbro. It was revised by San.ston Mdo.sde.dpal and Tshul.khrimş.dar (Toh.845).
Somanātha went to Magadha to study the Kālacakra under Kālacakraprāda Junior or Naropa.
He studied the Tibetan language and went to Tibet after the death of Atiśa. He had generous Tibetan
patrons who subsidised his translation work in the 11th century. As the script of the manuscript
shows it was written in Magadha and belongs to the early 11th century. It is the earliest manuscript of
the Vimalaprabhā. Jagannath Upadhyaya, Vrajavallabh Dvivedi and S.S. Bahulkar edited the
commentary and original Tantra in 1986-1994 from the Central Institute of Higher Tibetan Studies,
Sarnath. They used six manuscripts, three of them in Devanagari script, two in Newari script, and
one in old Bengaļi script. The present manuscript is the oldest of them, and merits a new edition.
The traditional chronology of the Kālacakra is as follows:
1. Šakyamuni appeared at Dhānyakataka in South India and preached the Kālacakra-tantra at
the request of King Sucandra from Sambhala near the Sītā River in Turkestan.
2. The next six kings of Sambhala continued the tradition.
3. The eighth King Mañjuśrīkīiti composed the shorter version in five chapters in 1,047 stanzas
from the long tantra in 12,000 stanzas. The extant version of the Kālacakra-tantra is the shorter one.
4. The subsequent kings were called Kulika or 'bearers of the lineage’. Kulika Puņdārīka wrote
the Vimalaprabhā commentary reproduced in this volume.
5. A Muslim invasion in 624 AD weakened the kingdom. It was 800 years after Kulika
Puņdarīka.
6. In 966 AD Chilupa of Orissa travelled to Sambhala and became versed in the root tantra and
its Vimalaprabhā commentary. Chilupa is the Kālacakrapāda Senior, while his disciple Naropa is
known as Kālacakrapāda Junior.
7. Naropa initiated Atīša into the Kalācakſa. Pindo or Pitopa became the prime disciple of Atīša.
8. Sixty years after Chilupa returned to India in 966, the Kālacakra was introduced into Tibet in
1026 AD.
9. Som.anātha a disciple of Naropa translated the Vimalaprabhā into Tibetan with the help of
Ses.rab.grags the Lotsava of Hbro. This transmission is known as the Lineage of Hbro.
10. The second transmission began with Rdo.rje.grags.pa the Lotsava of Rva. He studied the
Kālacakra in Kashmir under Samantaśrī for six years. The Rva lineage became important in the
Sa.skya denomination through Sa.skya Pandita (1182-1251) and his nephew Hphags.pa
Blo.gros.rgyal.mtshan (1235-1280).
11. Today it represents fundamental tenets of the Gelukpa denomination. His Holiness the Dalai
Lama XIV has been giving its empowerments around the world for several years and it has became
central to Tibetan Buddhism to transform body and mind into purity.
Sambhala on the Sīļā River or Syr Darya in East Turkestan seems to be a real geographic place.
The concept of Kālacakra presents common features with Zurvanism which was prevalent alongside
Zoroastrianism from the Achaemenian to the Sasanian empire. Achaemenes (Skt. Sakhāmaņi) the
ancestor of the Achaemenians lived in the eighth century BC. Cyrus the Great (ruled 559-530 BC),
began the uninterrupted Persian expansion of their rule. The last Achaemenian King Darius III
(r. 336-330) was routed by Alexander the Great at Arbela in 331 BC. The Sasanian dynasty reigned
from 224 to 651 AD. They inherited the territory, glory and Zoroastrian orthodoxy of the
Achaemenians as their descendants. While Zoroastrianism was the state religion, Zurvanism was a
parallel philosophical and religious thought. Zurwān (Avesta Zrvan) is the name of a deity in Pahlavi
sources. It is Zamān and means “Time'. Time is the central point of the mythology of the cult.
The Vendidad 19.29 distinguishes between “infinite Zurwān” and “finite Zurwān”. The word
Zurwān has cognates in the Rgveda 1.191.9 jūrv 'to consume by heat’, Rgveda jūryat, jurat
'to decay, perish', dhiyājur 'grown old in devotion' (Rgveda 5.43.15). The antiquity of Zurwanism
as a religious system s
stem spans several centuries. It must have been powerful in the peripheral regions of
the Iranian-speaking peoples. The Sītā River was on the rim of the Iranian lands. Deeply saturated
with Buddhism they created a syncretic deity of Kālacakra after the Islamic onslaught which
threatened all the minor beliefs alongwith Buddhism. The word Sambhala is derived from samvara
‘vow'→ śambara → śambhala. Kuļika Pundarīka was 800 years earlier than the Islamic invasion in
624 AD. It takes back the beginnings of the Kālacakra doctrine to 224 BC.
As Islam destroyed monasteries, smote statues, slew monks and slashed even the trees of the
şacred complexes, the sullen stones and depopulated santa knew only loneliness in the anger of
silence. Mind's geometry alive with the images of life, eternity playing in the purity of silence,
translated the faithless flush into a man-willed sacrament, into the image of Kālacakra. Assassination
of a millenarian culture travelled back in time in the deep-reaching mysteries of faith and the long
pilgrimage sank its roots in the Wheel of Time (Kāla-cakra) sans end. Muffled dreams became the
crystal hard determination to reincarnate in eternity. Like a wheel (cakra), Time (Kāla) is the timeless
movement where trampled dreams become incredible vitality. In Kālacakra, life and time, hope and
history, resolve and resurrection intertwine. Kālacakra is the reintegration of sacred time shattered by
sanctimonious time.
The Kālacakra was revealed, according to tradition, by the Buddha in the stūpa of
Dhānyakataka, twelve months after his enlightenment. The stūpa became dilated till it assumed the



In the Kālacakra rites, one performs the withdrawal of all appearances that melt
Into light and dissolve into myself.
I also melt into light and then from within
the emptiness of unapprehendability
Again transforms into the aspect of Kālacakra.
proportions of the universe. Sucandra wrote down the revelation, went back to his native country of
Śambhala, and built a stūpa in honour of the Kālacakra. The Tibetan tradition places Sambhala near
the Sītā River, that is, the Syr River in Central Asia. Many generations of Kulika kings ruled wisely
and handed down the teachings of Kālacakra. Their power was weakened by raids of mlecchas
(kla.klo) coming from Mecca (Me.kha), i.e. Muslim invasions. The Kulika king Rudracakrin will
defeat them and reinstatė the Dharma. The dharma-cakra becomes the Kāla-cakra: the eternal is
wounded in the flow of historical phenomena. The deeps of Buddhism, the infinite that upheld
(dhar-ma) the cosmic and human order is engulfed by the rising tide of Islam, Kālacakra is created as
a synthesis to ward off this threat. It is a new spiritual sensibility, a new value-centre to create new
determinants of power that flow from inner composuré. Kālacakrá seeks substance in time eternal.
On the philosophic level, Kālacakra “Wheel of Time” irradiates infinite expansion through three
planes, the physical, the verbal and the spiritual planes. The human mind needs the help of external
symbols to get a glimpse of the mystery behind and a guide on the path leading to it. Kālacakra is the
sign that reintegrates the lively inner experience of the roots of all things.
The consort of Kālacakra Viśvamātā wears a crown, which is of the nature of Vajrasattva.
She is adorned with the five types of ornaments, whereas Kālacakra himself has six types of
ornaments. The missing ornament on the consort is the one symbolizing the white bodhicitta.
The conjugal union of the deity and consort symbolises the union of method and wisdom. Kālacakra
symbolises method (upāya) which refers to the great bliss. The consort symbolises wisdom (prajñā)
which is the realization of emptiness. Theirs is the union of the great bliss and the wisdom realizing
emptiness. Without the wisdom of indivisible bliss and emptiness, it is impossible to reach the state
of full enlightenment. It is for this reason that Kālacakra symbolising method, and the consort
symbolising wisdom, are in intimate union.
In the Vimalaprabhā commentary, Kalacakra consists of emptiness and compassion, with
origination or annihilation in the three existences, the single image of knowledge and objects of
knowledge. He is embraced by Bhagavatī Prajñā or divine consort who is aspectless although
possessing aspect, the one possessing the unchanging bliss of the abandonment of origination and
annihilation. To attain the state of Buddhahood, manifesting as Kālacakra, one should identify
with and draw that into the present. One should meditate on the Kālacakra with an awareness of the
grëat good fortune of having opportunity to do so. Moreover, one should be free of the three faults of
a vessel:
Having a mind which is like an upside-down pot,
Having a mind which is like a pot with holes in it,
Having a mind which is like a pot that is dirty inside. .
The Kālacakra initiation makes manifest the fundamental innate mind of clear light, latent in all
experience. The sacred is the very essence of the profane. It is made profane by distortion. In the
initiation, the aspirant dissolves everything in emptiness, out of which re-appears a new dynamic
being: the paradox is that gain can come only from loss.
The five texts of the PANCARAKSĀ have been treated as separatė titles in the Kanjur (Toh. 558,
559, 561, 562, 563).
They were translated by Ye.ses.sde with the help of Śīlendrabodhi, Jñānasiddhi, Śākyaprabha,
Jinamitra and Dānaśīla, during the reign of Ral.pa.can who ruled from 817 to 836. It was a period of
great literary activity, when a common terminology was developed by a royal commission with
eminent Indian and Tibetan scholars for the translation of complex philosophic ideas. The outcome of
this historic effort was the Mahāvyutpatti, which is an astounding linguistic work of transforming a
primal Tibetan language into a valid literary language of Classical sophistication. The Sanskrit
manuscript of the five Raksā texts reproduced here should go back to the early ninth century. It is a
glorious symbol of the foundations of the literary heritage of Tibet.
The rich treasures of around a thousand Sanskrit manuscripts in Tibet from the ninth century
onwards is a legacy of humankind that deserves to be studied in international collaboration, like the
International Dunhuang Project in which the British Library, Dunhuang Institute and scholars from
all over the world are making the manuscripts accessible to research.
Lokesh Chandra

জgষণসান্ধবশ্ববিদ্যঃরঃ (ওস্লিব্রেত্রিবাে ছিধেখােকামুল কথাকাছি। ফঙেছোত্বিষী। ঋমেলিয়া সোফিয়জুনায়ে
.
স্বাগতষ্ঠাসূলাধার্তোবাঘথিংঘ@বেষণাৰি ৪ালগুলো কােম্পাঠিকান্দাইত্রাঘাষিস্তায় ফেWেষাঘাথেষঙ্গতি বােলাগালিবলেখেলাফললামঠাম্বােস/এবিমান
উেসচ্ছতাগুযঔছসিজিবিছালামাঞ্চেই অঙ্গাণ্ডায়মাঃ O অভিধাৰাৰিাষাশ্বযোগ্যসংশীৰ এইভেন্যUকমাবাই
২৪ভেকুলফাবিলাঞ্চলেঙ্গা ও নামফলমেফলতেষার্সোতোশাকশ্রাসোপেকৰষ্ঠান

এমােকাণাৰামনিহােমিওঠায়ঃঘাষনামূলমজোৰামৰফিৰমাগাযাতনামালামালকান্তমনিমােমোগ্রামগকিবঠনেমাযখোললাগুবিধাঃআমলাত্ৰীক্ষণওখাতে৷মধাভনে

ধাষেঠ৪ামকআতৰান্নাকাযােশােৰেত্তো আখামচেলমায়াযিবুধমুখাবোধলাঘনেশৱপ্ৰথমগুমাথা

যথে(ঠামােশনশিযেমcহ্মবিশ্বমাননাকাছি। . ওমওলাম্বলৰৰণামকোজিননকখামখেজনকাযযাম্বো } মােঃষ্টোমতােহ্মযােফোম্ভিওষকহেমন্মথ
তুখোমৃঠোলােচোৰাৰকৰেলৰাতঃৰাষাযমানাযােগোযযাকিশ্বমানবোকাসেমঠিযেহেযয়লেবেলায়েবেষকশকশ্রমেশে ১ ॥লমাঠমাঙামুঠিন্যেত্বে;
জস্বস্বমেহরঃধন্যারাগ্রামগুখোমুবিঠাখৃষীঠোঘাঁ৪ঠালবাঘিনমেম্বাবধিমাখযােঘালাখালগাছিন্নমগাওসুবিমলামেশাস্বষেণাসোস্কবাফ

এযেমৰমামাণযুধিৰিছিদ্বািযিঘাষযােবেঠম | গাভাস্কফেবৃন্যাযযােচ্ছে। এই নাম্বাঘোমাযফাযো৪েঃ খ
এম্বেবিন্নাঘ৪।বাহিমোফিসিয়ানফ্রাযোগঘোষাণির্মিঘযােবেবৈদ্যাধিবােতাসুমমেলবোের্সধামযিসমসাহাব।মাত্রাঙ্কস্ফোভিমুফাগুলােঃ
শৰাশৰস্বপনধিতস্কর্যযহাযথউসমান্বঘােষ্ঠিায়খদ্বিগুস্তাফালিস্রাদামুতেকালেসেনামায। মাস্কৰ্ম্মম্মম্ভহিকেওঠস্বলমেনস্ক
অদ্যাবাসনসিহাব।মামিজোব্রজছিয়গুলাে হলজিঘাবাজী২৪ ডমেওৰম্মুফজিম্বয়া

জামুকাথাও
৫ সেপ্লোমাসুমুসো ফালুকাৰােবাহিকঠিযমেণবষৰনকশেবামিওৰকৰীৰছায়ামামামামায়ামৰামফললারিবিষ্টসাক্ষাঙনযােগ্লারেস্তোরাই
| সুস্বাছিযখাশে৪েঠবাউছানেৰেহাইসগুলাই ও কাফফাহায়জেন্সিগুৰছিহমাধানমিষকালবানুৰাবেমেন্সেংঘ
অসহাৱাঠানমালা ভোমাসংঘ
* সুনাযোছৰািমইরহাদযেছিমহেবেথামা * সাম্রাজুঘর্যেস্থাষাৰাঘায়ােজঘঞ্চেছিবির্যমঞ্চ, ৩ পযৌফিকহ
বালবুয়েন্স'স্বক
বাল্লিযুযেমান্বগ্ৰহষাসুৰণস্বাভউকধমাঘকেযোমি
কালক্ষেমেষশুমাষামো।
স্বাণ্ডে!
দেখ:২৯ঠুযোসেম্বলিথোস্লোৰায়ঃবলেহাড়েম্বগ্নাছবিছাৰ্যামফিথ্রিথেলীমিস্ত্রিধাগ্রামাৰাধাকৃষ্ণষাযহাথষ্ণবয়েসয়াস।
কথপোযষ্ঠাবাঘgষ্টগােমাজিকষাঘধেছিবির্যাষক ও সাহিথেলাগ্লামানুসাফাঘিঝোনবপ্রেম্বেথীঘ্রায়
যেমন:

বিবঙ্গোএাঞ্চাযেৰবাশীনামাযাজৰ৪মোষেফেরমরমাণময়মৎSঘােহবিএমবোৰৰচমবঙ্গযবোনাৰণৰাযযাবলমৰেীযেeশেষেনভোযাথষযেন।
ওতাভস্বধাবোধতাকাযষযয়jে৪ঠাণাৰীশ্রীঠামশর্তনবাহনেয়ামকাঠিধাতবাঠেীদ্যাপাঠধাবেজম্বষেযঞ্চমবমেগবনমবযষঃশরণাল৪েঠঃষষ্ণবশত:
সুযােঙাম্বধাবিভ্রকেষ্ঠেযমুন্নোতেমঞ্চঘর্গন্মস্থানঃবধাযষীষ । স্বাধীনষেধাৰাথমিন্নাতক্ষযেবিমোঘমামধামচ ও লবশাখগাখনেমঃশ্বােঞ্চাখযমুনাত্তো )

মলয়াস্কোয়ামামাষ্টাৰাষ্ট্রেগুলেনোবে৷ংবোনেশ্মগোযসেবাযবোঠে৷৷সুয্যিায়বিদ্রোহবিলোমাবানেয়াহয়ঞ্জামিলধিঃগঠনেমাগ্রাফাৰ্মাকাবাল্যবিমgয়ার মাসযুরও কোয়া

মোবলামূৰ্কিনিষাষোবরেলবাসাখাতিঘোণীবিনষ্টকাৰাবাসাবাহান্নযােঘ্রথমেম্বাঠে৪াষতেনেহবে।

জিম্বন্ধষ্ঠায়মুঞ্জলসায়িকান্নাজায় অমর
दरलायनमिक्षालमनवेशवास्ता सजाउलानाशामा संगमावासमा
लिगवारमानितिनमाननवाजाभवाशीष दामाजमाखानामावतार मावा
निविदाशिवदत्तकाविशतावमलायाधिनान वानाक्षाचनपनाना
স্বকীখ্রিইনহালয়ামমোৰ স্বৈরাহিমু,
জুমাঃসুমহানামায়মুমুম্বদ্বেষঞ্জঞ্জিসুস্তুম্বুলেঞ্জেলসুম্বন্ধুগ্রখ্রত্যুত্ত স্থা
মুম্বজুয়রিয়াহী কাজী নীম্নগ্রাদলেয়ায়জামার যান্তিহল আজীবিতরিক্সায় জিহারী,
